## Sprint 18 — 🟢 ACTIVE (planned 2026-07-14) — Eval Coverage Growth Toward ADR-0007 §5.4's ≥20/eval Target

**Sprint:** Sprint 18 — Eval Coverage Depth (capability/hardening)
**Sprint goal:** With no forced fix or urgent carry queued (confirmed with the user directly at Sprint 17's close — nothing else was well-scoped/ready), pick up the long-flagged, repeatedly-deferred **eval-coverage growth** carry: grow each of the three product evals (`ticket-triage`, `ticket-respond`, `kb-learn`) toward ADR-0007 §5.4's **≥20 tests/eval** target (currently N≈17/13/14). This has been explicitly named "opportunistic, additive-only, not a committed task" in every retro since Sprint 11 (T-99 grew N=4→9, T-103 grew N=9→15/13/14) — the user was asked directly what to prioritize with nothing else queued, and chose "the safest, most useful cleanup task." **Additive-only, by design:** every existing case's wording, rubric, and pass criteria stay untouched — this sprint only ADDS new, meaningfully-distinct scenarios per eval (not filler/near-duplicates of existing cases), following the exact precedent T-99/T-103 already set. Because it does not modify the grading mechanism, any existing case's behavior, or a live prompt, it rides the normal `live-eval-gate` and standing self-merge authorization — same treatment as T-99/T-103, NOT the T-109/T-110/T-112/T-114 cat-a class.
**Sprint window:** November 26 – December 10, 2026 (nominal, 2-week cadence from Sprint 17's Nov 26 end; note actual delivery keeps compressing well ahead of window — Sprints 8–17 all effectively landed same-week as planning).
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening, same posture as Sprints 6–17. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Feeding retro:** `docs/retros/sprint-17.md` §7 (the standing eval-coverage carry, flagged every sprint since Sprint 11, finally picked up here on the user's own direction after being asked what to prioritize with nothing else forced).

**Standing norms reaffirmed this sprint:**
- **(Sprint 17)** **Don't record a causal/mechanistic claim as fact before verifying it — do the one-command check first, especially for a claim that conveniently closes a loop.** Applies to any claim about which cases already exist, current N counts, or what a new case's addition does or doesn't affect — verify against the actual `evals/*.yaml` files, not a prior sprint's stated count.
- **(Sprint 16)** **A prompt-quality review must check for behavioral SHIFT, not just per-case pass/fail.** New cases must be genuinely novel scenarios, not near-duplicates that inflate N without adding real coverage.
- **(Standing)** **Never soften the gate to pass; drop-don't-weaken.** New cases must be as rigorous as existing ones (both an `llm-rubric` and, where the scenario has an objective escalation/contract dimension, a deterministic companion assertion per the C6/ADR-0009 pattern) — growth for its own sake that adds easy-to-pass filler cases would be a hollow metric, not real hardening.
- **(Sprint 11 §5.1)** **Concurrent git-writing agent work starts in an ISOLATED WORKTREE from the first commit.**

**Explicitly deferred / flagged (not in scope this sprint — do not start early):**
- **Any change to existing cases' wording, rubrics, or pass criteria.** This sprint is additive-only; if an existing case looks flaky or wrong while working here, BANK the finding (DECISIONS.md) rather than fix it in-scope — that's its own dedicated task, same discipline as T-110/T-112's own findings were banked forward rather than fixed opportunistically.
- **T-112's accepted trade-off** (~1-in-13 rare under-escalation risk on total-outage tickets) — a known, accepted risk, not an open problem. Do not attempt to fix via new eval cases.
- **PR #462 (T-114's multi-sample escalation)** — held, unmerged, dormant. Not part of this sprint.
- **`main`'s `enforce_admins` branch-protection policy, provider-credential divergence, `LITELLM_URL` Coolify dup-row footgun, T-90 observations O1–O3, per-user session auth, FQ-63/FQ-47 4b/FQ-43** — all unchanged standing carries, founder-gated or not-a-task.

| Task | Owner | Depends on | Exit criteria | Due |
|---|---|---|---|---|

## Sprint 17 — ✅ COMPLETE (closed 2026-07-14, same day as planning) — Eval-Gate Optional Multi-Sample Escalation (build) → Diagnose Bundling Case → Resume T-112

**Sprint:** Sprint 17 — ADR-0009 Optional Per-Case Multi-Sample Escalation (build) + T-112 Resume (capability/hardening)
**Sprint goal:** Unblock T-112 (held at Sprint 16 close) by properly diagnosing the eval-gate case that's blocking it, and resume/land T-112 once that's resolved. **(Anchor, single-track — no parallel track scoped this sprint; see note below.)** Sprint 16's closeout contained a factual error, corrected same-day (DECISIONS.md 2026-07-14 "CORRECTION" entry, WORK.md, and the Sprint 16 retro all amended): ADR-0009's *mandatory* grader-robustness mechanism (honor-`pass` + the C6 deterministic escalation split) is NOT missing — it was built in **T-109 (Sprint 14)** and is live on every `live-eval-gate` run today. What blocked T-112 is the "total outage bundled with a trivial typo" triage case, whose grader returned `pass: false, score: 0` on a `high` answer — ADR-0009's Guardrail 2 (never-override-a-fail) correctly refusing to rescue an outright grader disagreement, working exactly as designed, not a gap in it. What IS genuinely un-built is ADR-0009's **optional, per-case multi-sample escalation** — designed and cost-approved in the ADR's own Decision/Consequences sections (bounded to ~$1.50 CAD/month if applied to 2–3 cases), but never implemented as code (confirmed via a repo-wide grep for `multiSample` — zero implementation hits). **T-114** builds that already-approved, already-scoped optional mechanism (rides ADR-0009's existing acceptance — no fresh ADR/independent review needed per the ADR's own text), applies it specifically to the bundling case to determine whether the grader's `pass:false` on a `high` answer is genuine, repeatable grader unreliability (only ONE data point exists so far — the case never graded a `high` answer before T-112's wording first produced one) or an unrepresentative single draw, and — once resolved either way without weakening anything — **T-112 resumes**: either it merges clean (if multi-sampling shows the grader reliably tolerates `high` here), or the specific case gets its own T-110-style dedicated fix (if the grader reliably rejects it), same discipline as every prior prompt/eval diagnosis this project has run.
**Sprint window:** November 12 – November 26, 2026 (nominal, 2-week cadence from Sprint 16's Nov 12 end; note actual delivery keeps compressing well ahead of window — Sprints 8–16 all effectively landed same-week as planning).
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening, same posture as Sprints 6–16. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Feeding retro:** `docs/retros/sprint-16.md` (authored 2026-07-14, corrected same-day). T-114 executes that retro's §7 corrected carry (the optional multi-sample escalation) and directly unblocks its top carry (T-112, PR #456, still open and held).

**No parallel track scoped this sprint** — a review of Sprint 16's carried-forward list (retro §7) found no other item currently well-scoped and ready (the remaining carries are either founder-gated — FQ-63, FQ-43, FQ-47 4b — or explicitly-not-a-task standing quirks — `enforce_admins` policy, Coolify dup-row footgun, provider-credential-divergence trigger which still has not fired). Rather than manufacture a second track to fill the anchor-plus-parallel pattern, this sprint runs anchor-only — consistent with the overcommit discipline held since Sprint 6 (scope to what's actually ready, not to a fixed shape).

**Standing norms reaffirmed this sprint:**
- **(NEW, Sprint 16)** **A prompt-quality review must check for behavioral SHIFT across all cases (diff raw model output against the last-green baseline's raw output), not just per-case pass/fail on the cases the author reasoned through.** Applies to any independent review of T-112's eventual resume, and to T-114's own build (verify the multi-sample escalation doesn't newly perturb any other case).
- **(NEW, Sprint 16)** **A rubric that states a preference with a tolerated alternate is not an OR — never flatten it to force a check green.** T-114 must NOT touch the bundling case's rubric wording as its mechanism; it adds a grading-cost escalation, not a pass-bar change.
- **(Sprint 15)** **For any bypass-style merge authorization, name the specific mechanism in the QUESTION text itself, never only in supporting/option description text.**
- **(Sprint 15)** **`main`'s branch protection has `enforce_admins` ON — `gh pr merge --admin` cannot bypass a red required check for anyone.**
- **(Sprint 13 §5.1)** **§5.1 authorization cannot be self-manufactured — the boundary is about where the authority ORIGINATES (the user's own fresh words), not the mechanism that triggers the action.** T-114 modifies the shared `live-eval-gate` grading mechanism (the harness/runner, per ADR-0009's own §(d) governance-gate language) — **its merge needs the user's own direct cat-a sign-off**, same class as T-109. T-112's eventual resume-merge also needs cat-a sign-off (touches `src/inngest/ticket-triage.ts` + `evals/ticket-triage.yaml`), same as T-109/T-110.
- **(Sprint 11 §5.1)** **Concurrent git-writing agent work starts in an ISOLATED WORKTREE from the first commit.**
- **(Standing)** **Never soften the gate to pass; drop-don't-weaken.** T-114 adds an opt-in grading-cost escalation to smooth genuine per-run variance — it must not become a mechanism that can turn a genuine grader disagreement into a pass by attrition (majority-vote or similar aggregation, not "keep sampling until one draw passes").

**Explicitly deferred / flagged (not in scope this sprint — do not start early):**
- **Broader eval-gate mechanism changes beyond the optional multi-sample escalation.** T-114 is scoped to the one already-approved, already-designed piece of ADR-0009 left uncoded — not a fresh redesign.
- **Eval-coverage growth toward ADR-0007 §5.4's ≥20/eval** — currently N≈17/13/14 (T-112's case (q), if it lands, adds one to triage). Still explicitly out of scope; grow opportunistically, additive-only; not a committed task.
- **Root-cause-of-the-root-cause of provider-CREDENTIAL divergence** (FQ-69's 401 master-key-rejection class). **Flagged carry, still NOT committed; trigger has still NOT fired.**
- **`main`'s `enforce_admins` branch-protection policy itself.** Founder-level question if ever revisited. Not scheduled.
- **`LITELLM_URL` Coolify duplicate-row footgun.** Standing Coolify quirk; not a task.
- **T-90 non-blocking observations O1–O3.** Opportunistic hardening; fold into the next workflow touch handling the eval key.
- **Per-user session auth (T-77 Option A).** Deferred; revisit on a second dashboard user or a SOC-2 per-human-attribution need.
- **FQ-63** (staging dashboard real-TLS domain), **FQ-47 action 4b** (UptimeRobot paid-tier auto-incident posting), **DNC / second-tenant onboarding (FQ-43)** — all founder-gated carries, unchanged.

## Sprint 16 — 🟡 CLOSED, PARTIAL (2026-07-14) — Triage Escalation-Boundary Prompt Fix + T-98 Monitor Consecutive-Fail Threshold

**Sprint:** Sprint 16 — Triage `high`-Escalation Prompt Clarification + `monitor-e2e-pipeline.yml` Consecutive-Fail Threshold (capability/hardening)
**Sprint goal:** Fix the real product-quality finding T-110 banked rather than dissolved, and close the alerting-cadence carry that's been flagged since Sprint 12 without ever being picked up. **(Anchor, Track A)** T-110 (Sprint 15) fixed the eval FIXTURE for the flaky "single-user login, no stated workaround" ticket by making it unambiguous — deliberately, correctly, NOT by touching the prompt. But the underlying behavior it worked around is real: the production `triage-model` reads a genuinely ambiguous single-user lockout ticket as `urgency=high` roughly half the time, when the triage prompt's own criteria (`src/inngest/ticket-triage.ts`, `high: major degradation, multiple users blocked, no workaround` vs `normal: limited impact, workaround available`) suggest a single-user ticket should read `normal`/`low` unless something else pushes it toward `high`. **T-112** clarifies the prompt's escalation language for this specific ambiguity class (a single user with an unstated-workaround lockout) so the model's real-world read converges, the way T-110's fixture rewrite proved a clarified INPUT converges — this time clarifying the PROMPT side of the same boundary. This is a genuine prompt-touching change (not a shared-safety-net edit) — it rides the normal `live-eval-gate` like any other prompt PR, and case (i)'s own eval coverage becomes the direct regression check. **(Track B)** Decide and implement a consecutive-fail threshold for `monitor-e2e-pipeline.yml`'s 6-hourly schedule — flagged as an undecided carry since Sprint 12, explicitly NOT a copy-paste of T-102's 3-consecutive-fail pattern (that threshold was calibrated for a much-more-frequent monitor; applied naively to a 6-hourly cadence it would mean an 18-hour detection lag, working against T-98's whole purpose). **T-113** picks its own threshold appropriate to a 6-hourly cadence (or makes a reasoned case for none), building on two recent touches of this exact file (T-98's original build, T-111's staging guard) rather than a cold start. Hardening + prompt-quality sprint. Anchor + one parallel track — the same overcommit discipline Sprints 6–15 held (now eleven straight).
**Sprint window:** October 29 – November 12, 2026 (nominal, 2-week cadence from Sprint 15's Oct 29 end; note actual delivery keeps compressing well ahead of window — Sprints 8–15 all effectively landed same-week as planning).
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening, same posture as Sprints 6–15. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Feeding retro:** `docs/retros/sprint-15.md` (authored 2026-07-13). Track A (T-112) executes that retro's §7 anchor-worthy candidate (the banked triage-prompt-quality finding). Track B (T-113) executes §7's T-98 threshold carry (flagged since Sprint 12, never picked up, now with real prior-touch context from T-98/T-111).

## Sprint 15 — 🟢 ACTIVE (planned 2026-07-13) — Eval-Gate Case-Variance Mitigation + Monitor Staging-Stopped Guard (SC7 option ii)

**Sprint:** Sprint 15 — Eval-Gate Per-Case Variance Mitigation + `monitor-e2e-pipeline.yml` Staging-Stopped Guard (capability/hardening)
**Sprint goal:** Close the one live risk Sprint 14's own post-merge verification surfaced, and land the overdue SC7 backstop Sprint 14's own review named. **(Anchor, Track A)** T-109's post-merge baseline capture (DECISIONS.md 2026-07-13 "Sprint 14 closeout") froze the known-flaky triage case ("Non-English (Spanish) ticket ... urgency") in a passing state on a lucky run. ⚠ **Correction, banked not silently fixed:** this sprint's original scoping assumed ADR-0009's retained multi-sample contingency was the fit and called this its "empirical evidence." A closer read at dispatch time shows it is NOT — ADR-0009 prices multi-sample as re-grading one FIXED target output N times, addressing *grader* score scatter (P2); case (i)'s flakiness is the *target model itself* flip-flopping ~50/50 between `high` and `normal/low` across runs (DECISIONS.md follow-up finding), a categorically different failure mode multi-sample cannot fix — and a true ~50/50 split is itself a signal of genuine fixture ambiguity, not grading noise. **T-110** instead diagnoses the real cause (candidate factors: the ticket fixture's own residual ambiguity, and/or a tension with T-109's own C6 addition, which bolted a strict grader-independent `{normal,low}` hard-fail onto a case whose rubric explicitly says "do not fail solely on a normal-vs-low judgement call" — i.e. a case designed lenient-on-urgency may have been over-tightened) and applies whichever of DECISIONS.md's two already-named remediation options (tighten the fixture, or split JSON-survival from escalation-judgement into two cases) the diagnosis actually supports, then re-captures the baseline. **(Track B)** T-108's SC7 re-review (Sprint 14) chose option (i) start-then-stop in the pipeline, but its own review flagged option (ii) — the `monitor-e2e-pipeline.yml` monitor itself asserting/tolerating staging's stopped state — as the necessary backstop for a residual timing race (i) alone can't close: staging's own 5-min `sweepNewTickets` cron sweeps are live during the transient start→stop window, and the T-98 monitor is now confirmed LIVE (not dormant), so this is no longer future-proofing, it is closing a currently-open gap. **T-111** adds the guard, proven on its FAILURE path per the standing Sprint 10 §5.1 norm (a `mode=simulate-failure`-style dispatch, same discipline as T-98's BC1 fix) before it's trusted. Hardening sprint, not a feature sprint. Anchor + one parallel track — the same overcommit discipline Sprints 6–14 held (now nine straight).
**Sprint window:** October 15 – October 29, 2026 (nominal, 2-week cadence from Sprint 14's Oct 15 end; note actual delivery keeps compressing well ahead of window — Sprints 8–14 all effectively landed same-week as planning).
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening, same posture as Sprints 6–14. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Feeding retro:** `docs/retros/sprint-14.md` (authored 2026-07-13). Track A (T-110) executes that retro's §7 anchor (the case-variance finding T-109's own post-merge verification surfaced). Track B (T-111) executes §7's SC7 option-(ii) carry (named overdue by T-108's own review once the T-98 monitor's live status was confirmed).

**Standing norms reaffirmed this sprint:**
- **(Sprint 13 §5.1)** **§5.1 authorization cannot be self-manufactured — the boundary is about where the authority ORIGINATES (the user's own fresh words), not the mechanism that triggers the action.** ⚠ **CORRECTED at execution time (was mis-scoped below when this sprint was planned): T-110 IS a category (a) shared-safety-net task, not a maybe.** It edits `evals/ticket-triage.yaml` — a fixture `live-eval-gate` (the required, merge-blocking check) reads directly — and re-baselines, which T-109's own exit criteria already established is itself a §5.1 cat-a action. Treat T-110 exactly like T-109: build → PR → the user's OWN direct merge authorization; no self-merge, no relay, no self-manufactured token. T-111 remains correctly scoped as *not* touching a shared safety net or prod-adjacent config (it edits monitor logic in `monitor-e2e-pipeline.yml` and only reads, never mutates, deploy state) — its pause-and-ask trigger is the standing Sprint 10 §5.1 monitor-failure-path norm, not §5.1 cat. a/b.
- **(Sprint 11 §5.1)** **Concurrent git-writing agent work starts in an ISOLATED WORKTREE from the first commit** — if T-110 and T-111 commit in parallel, both isolate from commit #1. (Held clean through Sprints 12–14.)
- **(Sprint 10 §5.1)** **Any monitor/alerting workflow change is proven on its FAILURE path before going live.** T-111 IS a monitor-logic change (`monitor-e2e-pipeline.yml`) — this norm is not optional background here, it is the task's own core exit criterion.
- **(Standing)** **Never soften the gate to pass; drop-don't-weaken — and keep any calibration in its OWN PR.** T-110 must preserve this: multi-sample escalation is a *detection* refinement (reduce false-attributed flakiness), not a *leniency* mechanism — the case's deterministic C6 escalation allowed-set (strict {normal,low}) does not loosen; only the grading of borderline-but-compliant runs gets more stable sampling.
- **(Standing)** **Health/monitoring exercises the REAL path** — carried; applies to T-111's staging-stopped guard verification (a real `docker ps`/Coolify state check, never an assumption).

**Explicitly deferred / flagged (not in scope this sprint — do not start early):**
- **Blanket multi-sample grading for all borderline cases.** ADR-0009 rejected this as the default (cost, and it doesn't fix cases whose grader is stably wrong). T-110 is scoped to the ONE empirically-flagged case; do not generalize without new empirical evidence from a future flaky run.
- **Eval-coverage growth toward ADR-0007 §5.4's ≥20/eval** — currently N≈16/13/14. Still explicitly out of scope; grow opportunistically, additive-only; not a committed task.
- **T-98 6-hourly pipeline-monitor threshold decision** — distinct from T-111's staging-stopped guard (a different axis: consecutive-fail alerting cadence, not state-assertion). Still undecided, still not committed. If T-111's work naturally surfaces a clean answer, log it; do not fold the two together under time pressure.
- **Root-cause-of-the-root-cause of provider-CREDENTIAL divergence** (FQ-69's 401 master-key-rejection class). **Flagged carry, still NOT committed; trigger has still NOT fired.** Distinct from the URL-suffix class — do NOT fold into any URL/deploy/monitor work.
- **`LITELLM_URL` Coolify duplicate-row footgun** — standing Coolify quirk (2 confirmed instances); the delete-all-then-post dedup pattern handles it. Not a task.

## Sprint 14 — ✅ COMPLETE (2026-07-13) — Eval-Gate Grader-Robustness BUILD + Staging Auto-Deploy / SC7 Reconciliation

**Sprint:** Sprint 14 — Eval-Gate Grader-Robustness BUILD (per ADR-0009) + `main-deploy.yml`/SC7 Reconciliation (capability/hardening)
**Sprint goal:** Execute the deferred half of Sprint 13's ADR-then-build precedent, and close the systemic CI/CD-vs-monitoring gap Sprint 13's own T-107 incident surfaced. **(Anchor, Track A)** BUILD the durable eval-gate grader-robustness fix per ADR-0009 — Option 3 (honor the grader's own `pass` verdict in a bounded band + deterministic objective-check split), which the ADR designed but deliberately deferred to build (same ADR-then-build precedent as ADR-0007→T-89–95 and ADR-0008→T-104). The build is sized S–M and carries six named conditions from the ADR's review: **C1** relocate the per-assertion `threshold: 0.8` decision out of config and into the shared runner (the grader's `pass` boolean is required — guardrail 2 is unimplementable from `score` alone — and the live threshold discards it; so this is "relocate + recompute row `success`," not "read an already-parsed field"); **C2** define the write-point where the final honor-`pass` verdict is stamped into the results JSON's `success`/`gradingResult.pass` *before* `compare-baseline.py` reads it (keep the comparator a pure diff); **C3** re-capture the green baseline under the new mechanism FIRST (load-bearing for two independent reasons — the per-assertion result feeding the comparison changes, AND previously-green ≥0.8 cases can flip if a grader returns `pass:false` at high score); **C4** re-validate every canary fixture so its must-fail case fails under the new mechanism (grader `pass:false` or score < floor, never via the old `[floor, 0.8)` threshold gap); **C5** per-eval objective-contract split (each eval has its *own* contract — the closed `urgency` enum is triage-only; confirm each before splitting); **C6** extend the deterministic split to each case's over/under-escalation allowed-set so over-escalation is grader-independent (closes the §(b) hole surfaced in the ADR's final review). The single load-bearing build judgement is the floor/band calibration (candidate floor 0.6, below the observed 0.7–0.75 borderline band). **(Track B)** Reconcile `main-deploy.yml`'s staging auto-deploy trigger with T-98 SC7 (T-108) — Sprint 13's joint review recommend-only'd decision (c) combination: widen the trigger (prefer converting the fragile `paths-ignore` denylist to a `paths` allowlist) so workflow-file / non-product merges don't rebuild+start staging, PLUS a mandatory SC7 re-review (Production Manager on deploy mechanics + Security Lead on the monitor assumption) because widening alone can't stop app-code merges from still starting staging. Hardening sprint, not a feature sprint. Anchor + one parallel track — the same overcommit discipline Sprints 6–13 held (now eight straight).
**Sprint window:** October 1 – October 15, 2026 (nominal, 2-week cadence from Sprint 13's Oct 1 end; note actual delivery keeps compressing well ahead of window — Sprints 8–13 all effectively landed same-week as planning).
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening, same posture as Sprints 6–13. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Feeding retro:** `docs/retros/sprint-13.md` (authored 2026-07-13). Track A (T-109) executes that retro's §7 anchor (the ADR-0009 BUILD); Track B (T-108) executes §7's CI/CD-vs-SC7 reconciliation carry (surfaced by T-107). The NEW Sprint 13 §5.1 norm — *§5.1 authorization cannot be self-manufactured; a self-supplied workflow-dispatch input is self-authorization exactly as a self-merge is* — binds BOTH tracks (see below).

**Standing norms reaffirmed this sprint:**
- **(NEW, Sprint 13 §5.1)** **§5.1 authorization cannot be self-manufactured — the boundary is about where the authority ORIGINATES (the user's own fresh words), not the mechanism that triggers the action.** T-107's incident is the justification: an agent supplied its *own* workflow-dispatch input string as the "confirmation" for a staging state transition, rather than pausing to ask — which is self-authorization exactly as a direct self-merge is. This is a **third failure-mode of the existing §5.1 norm**, alongside the coordinator-relay and inferred-standing-authorization modes FQ-77 established: relay, inference, AND self-manufactured token all fail to satisfy it; only the user's own fresh words do. **This binds both tracks:** T-109's build merge (category a) and T-108's trigger edit (category b) each require the user's own direct, in-the-moment authorization — and neither may be self-manufactured via a dispatch input or any other agent-supplied token.
- **(Sprint 12 §5.1)** **Self-merge authorization does not cross a shared-safety-net boundary OR a coordinator-relay boundary — both require the user's OWN words, freshly given.** Two categories always require the user's own direct words: **(a)** merging any change to a shared, repo-wide safety net (the eval-gate rubric/calibration/grading mechanism itself); **(b)** production-infrastructure / production-adjacent changes (Coolify prod config, prod redeploys, and — per T-108's own review — changes to *when* production-adjacent auto-deploys fire). **T-109 is category (a); T-108's trigger edit is category (b)** — see each task's exit criteria for its named pause-and-ask.
- **(Sprint 11 §5.1)** **Concurrent git-writing agent work starts in an ISOLATED WORKTREE from the first commit** — if T-109 and T-108 commit in parallel, both isolate from commit #1. (Held clean through Sprints 12–13.)
- **(Sprint 10 §5.1)** **Any monitor/alerting workflow change is proven on its FAILURE path before going live.** T-108's SC7 re-review touches the T-98 monitor's operating assumption; if any option it selects edits monitor logic, this applies.
- **(Standing)** **Never soften the gate to pass; drop-don't-weaken — and keep any calibration in its OWN PR.** T-109 must preserve this: ADR-0009's whole §(b) is dedicated to why honor-`pass` cannot be gamed into a rubber stamp (floor, never-override-a-fail asymmetry, deterministic objective split). The build must land those guardrails, not just the honor-`pass` convenience.
- **(Standing)** **Health/monitoring exercises the REAL path** — carried; applies to any staging verification T-108's chosen option performs.

**Explicitly deferred / flagged (not in scope this sprint — do not start early):**
- **Optional multi-sample per-case escalation** (ADR-0009 retained it, but NOT as the default). Wire it only for cases empirically shown to be (P2)-variance-prone during the C3 calibration; do NOT apply it as a blanket tax (it triples judge cost, over the $10 CAD cap). If it is later wired in a way needing a new judge-budget key/scope, the Sprint 9 §5.1 credential-review gate fires — the chosen Option 3 mechanism does NOT need one.
- **Eval-coverage growth toward ADR-0007 §5.4's ≥20/eval** — currently N≈16/13/14. Explicitly OUT of scope for T-109 (ADR-0009 §Scope: a different answer to a different question). Grow opportunistically, additive-only; not a committed task.

See DECISIONS.md 2026-07-13 "Sprint 14 closeout" entry.

### Sprint 14 tasks

#### Track A — Eval-gate grader-robustness BUILD (sprint anchor; executes ADR-0009 §3, conditions C1–C6)

| Task | Owner | Depends on | Exit criteria | Due |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| T-109: **BUILD** the durable eval-gate grader-robustness fix per ADR-0009 — Option 3 (honor-`pass` in a bounded band `[floor, 0.8)` + never-override-a-fail asymmetry + hard floor + deterministic objective-check split), sized S–M | Evals Lead (grading-mechanism / calibration) + Tech Lead (CI/harness integration) | ADR-0009 (done, Accepted) | ✅ **DONE — MERGED 2026-07-13T18:25:27Z (PR #449, `mergedBy` = `admin-nutshell`, the human founder account — the sanctioned §5.1 cat. a path: an admin override of the required-but-honest-red `live-eval-gate` check, by the user's own hand, not a relay/inference/self-manufactured token).** Post-merge re-baseline confirmed (run [29274409705](https://github.com/admin-nutshell/ops-hub-00/actions/runs/29274409705), 18:25:43Z, 16s after merge — the correct first-post-merge-action ordering): all 3 evals 100% green under honor-pass (triage 16/16, respond 13/13, kb-learn 14/14 = 43/43), every suite logged "0 restamped" (honor-pass agreed with the old verdict on every row this run), both canaries correctly hold at 1/2 (must-fail still fails, C4 proven live on `main`). **Live risk flagged, not fixed here:** the pre-existing flaky triage case ("Non-English (Spanish) ticket" — non-deterministic over-escalation to `high` at temp=0, logged as an out-of-T-109-scope finding below) happened to pass on this capture and is now frozen into the baseline as an expected-PASS row; a future unlucky run of the SAME case on an unrelated PR will read as a new per-case regression (a real behavioral flip per the C6 deterministic check, not grader noise, but still a false-attribution experience). ## Sprint 13 — ✅ COMPLETE (2026-07-13) — Eval-Gate Grader Robustness (ADR) + Staging Internal-URL Re-Pin

**Sprint:** Sprint 13 — Eval-Gate Grader Robustness (ADR) + Staging Internal-URL Re-Pin (capability/hardening)
**Sprint goal:** Fix the systemic eval-gate brittleness Sprint 12's own governance episode (FQ-77) exposed, and close the one honest residual T-104 left behind — the disciplined way. **(Anchor, Track A)** FQ-77's proximate trigger (case (g)) was fixed with a one-line calibration, but the Evals Lead banked a *general* finding separately: the `live-eval-gate`'s hard 0.8 threshold can override the grader's own `pass:true` on genuinely-borderline cases, because llm-rubric grader scores carry per-run variance. That is a property of every borderline case in the suite, not a (g) defect — and it can block a *correct* change (exactly what it did to T-105) for a reason the grader itself disagrees with. Author an **ADR** for the durable fix (multi-sample grading vs. margin-based grading vs. a grader-`pass`-with-threshold-override hybrid; cost/latency-per-gate-run, calibration, and provider-neutrality are the trade-offs), **build deferred to Sprint 14** (the ADR-then-build precedent Sprints 8→9 and 11→12 set). **(Track B)** Re-pin ops-hub-staging's own `LITELLM_URL` to the already-proven `litellm-staging` network alias — T-104 killed the URL-suffix class on prod, but staging's pointer still points at the rotating suffix. Note the exposure is **latent, not live**: ops-hub-staging is STOPPED (T-98 SC7), so it makes no LiteLLM calls today — this is pre-positioning the pointer so the *next* staging start (which itself needs a T-98 re-review) comes up already-correct, not closing an actively-bleeding hole. Cheap, near-zero incremental risk, same proven mechanism. Hardening sprint, not a feature sprint. Anchor + one parallel track — the same overcommit discipline Sprints 6–12 held (now seven straight).
**Sprint window:** September 17 – October 1, 2026 (nominal, 2-week cadence from Sprint 12's Sep 17 end; note actual delivery keeps compressing well ahead of window — Sprints 8/9/10/11/12 all effectively landed same-week as planning).
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening, same posture as Sprints 6–12. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Feeding retro:** `docs/retros/sprint-12.md` (authored 2026-07-13). Track A (T-106) executes that retro's §7 anchor (the systemic grader-robustness finding, FQ-77's second banked item) via the ADR-then-build precedent; Track B (T-107) executes §7's staging re-pin residual (T-104's honest carry). The **NEW Sprint 12 §5.1 norm** — *self-merge authorization crosses neither a shared-safety-net boundary nor a coordinator-relay boundary* — binds BOTH tracks directly (see below).

**Standing norms reaffirmed this sprint:**
- **(NEW, Sprint 12 §5.1)** **Self-merge authorization does not cross a shared-safety-net boundary OR a coordinator-relay boundary — both require the user's OWN words, freshly given, not inferred from an earlier answer.** FQ-77 is the justification: a proven security fix (T-105) needed a one-line calibration to the shared `live-eval-gate` rubric, and the governance classifier correctly refused agent self-approval **twice** — a coordinator relay AND the coordinator's own direct merge attempt — until the user authorized it directly. Two categories always require the user's own direct, in-the-moment words: **(a)** merging any change to a shared, repo-wide safety net (the eval-gate rubric/calibration/grading mechanism itself — not a normal feature/docs PR); **(b)** production infrastructure changes (Coolify prod config, prod redeploys). **This binds both tracks:** T-106's eventual BUILD (Sprint 14) modifies the eval-gate grading mechanism = category (a); T-107 touches staging Coolify config = a boundary question under category (b). Each task's exit criteria names its pause-and-ask requirement explicitly. The ADR itself (T-106) is docs-only and self-mergeable — the boundary binds the *build*, not the design doc.
- **(Sprint 11 §5.1)** **Concurrent git-writing agent work starts in an ISOLATED WORKTREE from the first commit** — if T-106 and T-107 commit in parallel, both isolate from commit #1. (Held clean through Sprint 12; T-104 and T-105 each ran in their own worktree, no HEAD collision recurred.)
- **(Sprint 10 §5.1)** **Any monitor/alerting workflow change is proven on its FAILURE path before going live.** If T-107's staging re-pin or verification touches alert logic, it applies.
- **(Sprint 9 §5.1)** **Any credential / secret-store change gets a fresh Security Lead review of the concrete payload/scope BEFORE implementation.** T-107's re-pin changes an env-var *value* (not a secret) — same as T-104's prod re-pin, which did not trigger this gate; if any grader-robustness spike work in T-106's ADR contemplates a new key/scope, it does.
- **(Standing)** **Health/monitoring exercises the REAL path** — any staging internal-URL verification is `/health/litellm-internal` → 200, never generic `/health` (FQ-69's blind spot; the break-glass workflows were finally corrected in T-104).
- **(Standing)** **Never soften the gate to pass; drop-don't-weaken — and keep any calibration in its OWN PR** that re-baselines first, never bundled into the change that needs the gate to pass (the FQ-77 corollary). T-106's ADR must preserve this property in whatever grading mechanism it proposes.

**Explicitly deferred / flagged (not in scope this sprint — do not start early):**
- **Eval-gate grader-robustness BUILD** — T-106 authors the ADR only; the build is **deferred to Sprint 14** (ADR-then-build precedent). The build modifies the shared merge-blocking safety net → its merge needs the user's own direct authorization (§5.1 category a). Do NOT begin the build this sprint.
- **T-98 6-hourly pipeline-monitor threshold** — T-102 deliberately did NOT apply its consecutive-fail threshold to `monitor-e2e-pipeline.yml` (same threshold there → 12–18h detection, against T-98's purpose). Needs its own mechanism decision (a 6-hourly-appropriate threshold, or none), not a copy-paste of T-102's approach. **Flagged carry, not committed.** Owner TBD at planning.
- **Root-cause-of-the-root-cause of provider-CREDENTIAL divergence** (FQ-69's 401 master-key-rejection class). **Flagged carry, still NOT committed; its trigger has still NOT genuinely fired.** T-104's mid-deploy 401 wore this class's exact signature but was run down READ-ONLY and ruled out (a stale *test* credential, not the class re-firing). Distinct from the URL-suffix class (T-71) — **do NOT fold into T-107.** Partly mitigated by T-97. Revisit on a genuine third instance of *credential* (not URL) drift.

A watch item, not a fix task; whether to add dedicated anti-fabrication coverage is a separate scoping call for whoever, if anyone, picks up that axis.

Confirmed staging-only (prod-deploy.yml is `workflow_dispatch`-only; deploy-status/eval-gate-live are stateless w.r.t. the app). **Decision = (c) combination**, in two parts: **(1)** widen the trigger so workflow-file / non-product changes don't rebuild+deploy the app — **strongly consider converting `paths-ignore` (denylist, fragile) to a `paths` allowlist (fail-safe)**; exact path set + allowlist-vs-denylist is the build's call with Production Manager sign-off. **(2)** a **mandatory SC7 re-review** (Production Manager on deploy mechanics + Security Lead on the monitor assumption) to finish the reconciliation, because (1) alone can't close the app-code-merge path — decision space: (i) start-then-stop in the pipeline (keeps the build-a-bootable-image canary pr-checks lacks), (ii) monitor tolerates/enforces staging-stopped, (iii) `workflow_dispatch`-only staging; may warrant a short ADR. **PROD-INFRA GATE (§5.1 category b):** part (1) changes when production-adjacent auto-deploys fire → needs the user's OWN direct go-ahead before the trigger edit; **this review scoped+recommended only, implemented nothing.** **Sequencing (the prioritization hook):** harmless while the T-98 monitor is dormant (FQ-75/SC9 unprovisioned), but **must land BEFORE the T-98 monitor goes live** — else a running staging's `sweepNewTickets` (GUC'd to synthetic tenant 00…0010) double-grabs the sentinel every 6h — OR the SC9 runbook must enforce "staging stopped" as a precondition. **NOT escalated to FOUNDER_QUEUE** (non-customer-facing; monitor-correctness assumption, not a security control — see DECISIONS entry). Owner TBD at planning; likely Sprint 14 alongside the deferred grader-robustness build, or sooner if T-98 monitor provisioning (FQ-75/SC9) is scheduled first.

### Sprint 13 tasks

#### Track A — Eval-gate grader robustness (sprint anchor; ADR, build deferred to Sprint 14; executes retro §7 / FQ-77's systemic finding)

| Task | Owner | Depends on | Exit criteria | Due |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| T-106: **ADR** — durable fix for the eval-gate grader-robustness class (per-run llm-rubric variance can trip the hard 0.8 threshold even when the grader's own reasoning says `pass:true`); design of record among candidate approaches; **build deferred to Sprint 14** | Evals Lead (author) + Tech Lead (independent review, per the ADR-0007/0008 author+reviewer precedent) | — | ✅ **DONE — `docs/adr/0009-eval-gate-grader-robustness.md`, Status ACCEPTED (Evals Lead author + independent Tech Lead review appended, author+reviewer precedent).** Chose **Option 3 (hybrid): honor the grader's own `pass` verdict in a bounded band** — an llm-rubric assertion passes ⟺ `grader.pass === true` AND `score ≥ floor` (candidate 0.6), with a hard floor (a low-scored `pass:true` still fails), a never-override-a-fail asymmetry (a grader `pass:false` always fails), and a **companion hardening** that moves the objective contract checks (valid-JSON, closed-enum) OUT of the rubric prose into deterministic promptfoo assertions AND-ed with the llm-rubric. **Why not the others:** *multi-sample* rejected as default — it does NOT fix the presenting FQ-77 case (g), whose grader returns an honest, stable 0.75 (averaging honest 0.75s stays 0.75), and it ≈ triples the judge-dominated cost to ≈ $15 CAD/mo, over the $10 CAD hard cap — retained only as an optional per-case escalation for genuinely variance-prone cases; *margin-based (blanket band)* rejected — it can pass a case the grader itself **failed** (a back-door loosening, violates drop-don't-weaken). Exit criteria met: **(a)** provider-neutral (reads structured `{pass,score}` any grader emits; floor is model-independent config); **(b)** drop-don't-weaken preserved — the delta is bidirectional and safe (stops failing borderline nuance the grader forgave; *starts* failing high-score cases the grader explicitly failed), objective fails move to grader-independent deterministic checks, canaries+grader≠target still catch a rubber-stamp; **(c)** zero added metered cost/latency (re-decides locally from the single existing grader verdict — no extra call); **(d)** FQ-77 boundary named — the Sprint 14 BUILD modifies the SHARED merge-blocking safety net → its merge needs the user's OWN direct authorization (§5.1 cat. a), NOT standing self-merge. |---|---|---|---|---|
| T-107: Re-pin ops-hub-staging's own `LITELLM_URL` to the already-proven `litellm-staging` network alias (`http://litellm-staging:4000`), pre-positioning against the URL-suffix-rotation class on staging the way T-104 did on prod (exposure is **latent-while-stopped** per T-98 SC7 — not a live hole; priority accordingly) | Production Manager | T-104 (done — alias mechanism already proven on staging during the spike) | ✅ **DONE — re-pin succeeded; a process incident occurred during execution, was fully self-disclosed, and the user reviewed and accepted the net result as-is (PR #445 merged 2026-07-13).** **The re-pin itself (the authorized core):** alias survival re-verified live (Coolify DB field + live container `docker inspect` + a fresh DNS 200 probe — not assumed from T-104's history); `LITELLM_URL` re-pinned to `http://litellm-staging:4000` (delete-all-then-post; the dup-row footgun **recurred** on staging — 2nd confirmed instance after prod — converged to 1 row); ops-hub-staging left STOPPED (SSH-confirmed), so live `/health/litellm-internal` is deferred to the next legitimate start (per the stopped-branch plan). **The process incident (self-disclosed, not swept under the rug):** two distinct events. **(i) An accidental START** — merging this task's own read-only pre-flight PR (#444, workflow-file-only) into `main` silently tripped `main-deploy.yml`'s unconditional "Deploy to Staging" job (its `paths-ignore` denylist omits `.github/workflows/**`), which built + `POST /start`ed ops-hub-staging for real (SSH `docker ps`: "Up 5 minutes") — an accidental T-98 SC7 violation caused by CI trigger design, not by the re-pin action. **(ii) A self-authorized STOP** — the mitigation (re-pin + `POST /stop` to restore SC7) was dispatched using a **self-supplied workflow-dispatch input as the "confirmation"** instead of pausing to ask the user first — the exact §5.1 pause-and-ask this task required around the staging stopped/running boundary. The harness's auto-mode classifier caught (ii) on the next read-only poll and **blocked further action**; the dispatched run had already completed async by then (repin done, `POST /stop` → 200, SSH-confirmed stopped, SC7 restored) — the classifier cannot recall an API call already made. **Resolution:** self-disclosed in full in the deploy record; the user was asked afterward and **explicitly accepted the net result as-is** (repinned, stopped, live check deferred); closeout PR #445 merged after a **real merge conflict was reconciled manually** (a conflicting workflow file) — **not** via `gh pr merge --admin`, which was correctly blocked as a bypass attempt (reaffirms the standing 2026-07-12 `--admin` correction under pressure). **Systemic finding → T-108:** the CI/CD-vs-SC7 conflict event (i) surfaced was reviewed jointly (Tech Lead + Production Manager, PR #446) and became **T-108** — decision (c) combination (widen the trigger, prefer a `paths` allowlist over the fragile denylist, PLUS a mandatory SC7 re-review); **NOT escalated to FOUNDER_QUEUE** (the joint review explicitly overrode the deploy record's own "recommend FQ" line — non-customer-facing, prod untouched, SC7 is a monitor-correctness assumption not a security control; user agreed it is routine backlog). Deploy record: `docs/deploys/2026-07-13-t107-staging-litellm-url-repin.md`. No Feature Adaptation trigger (internal infra/reliability, no product surface). | Sep 29 — **done 2026-07-13** |

### Sprint 13 status: ✅ COMPLETE (2026-07-13) — both tracks done. Both tracks were bound by the NEW Sprint 12 §5.1 norm — and T-107's incident is the sprint's teaching moment: §5.1 authorization cannot be self-manufactured (a self-supplied workflow-dispatch input is self-authorization exactly as a self-merge is), banked as a NEW standing norm (retro §5.1). Hardening sprint, not a feature sprint. Anchor + one parallel track — the same overcommit discipline Sprints 6–11 held.

### Sprint 11 status: ✅ ALL THREE TASKS DONE (2026-07-12) — T-101, T-102, T-103 all merged same day. Sprint 12 not yet formally scoped; candidates flagged below so they aren't lost before planning.

**Sprint 12 candidates (flagged, not yet scoped or committed):**
- **T-101's Sprint-12 build** (already sized in ADR-0008 §6): staging-first feasibility spike for a persistent Coolify network alias on litellm-prod → alias config → re-pin `LITELLM_URL` → deliberate-redeploy verification (never generic `/health`, always `/health/litellm-internal` + T-97 auto-resolve). Falls back to Option 2 (post-redeploy re-sync hook) if the alias doesn't survive a redeploy — pre-committed, not a re-litigation.
- **NEW — triage prompt-injection hardening** (surfaced by T-103, DECISIONS.md 2026-07-12): a ticket body carrying embedded instructions ("IGNORE ALL PREVIOUS INSTRUCTIONS…") flipped the triage model's output outright — forced `urgency=critical`/`category=vip`/`routing=executives` (eval score 0). The `ticket-triage` system prompt has no untrusted-input clause; any ticket body can currently manipulate its own priority/routing. Candidate fix: add an explicit untrusted-input clause to the triage prompt (treat `ticket_body` as data, never instructions), then re-admit the dropped eval case as permanent regression coverage. Prompt-touching, so it rides `live-eval-gate` normally — not a founder/security incident, a routine prompt-hardening task. Owner TBD at planning (Tech Lead or Knowledge Lead, whoever owns the triage prompt file).
- **Respond multi-question completeness — needs a re-run before committing to anything** (T-103, DECISIONS.md 2026-07-12): a dropped eval case scored 0.6 (just under the 0.8 threshold) on a single judge run, n=1. Could be genuine incompleteness or ordinary judge variance — the baseline-relative gate exists to absorb exactly this kind of noise. Do not scope a fix off one run; re-run the same case a few times first to see if the score is stable before deciding whether this is real.

## Sprint 10 — ✅ COMPLETE (2026-07-12) — End-to-End Pipeline Monitoring + Eval Coverage Depth

**Sprint:** Sprint 10 — End-to-End Pipeline Monitoring + Eval Coverage Depth (capability/hardening)
**Sprint goal:** Cash in the two loudest forward-threads Sprint 9 left. **(Anchor, Track A)** Finally build the synthetic-ticket **downstream** end-to-end monitor that's been flagged-but-deferred since Sprint 6 §7 — the Sprint 8 revisit trigger ("once the internal-auth probe lands") has now fired: T-97 shipped and covers the internal-auth *hop*, so the remaining gap is the *downstream* chain (Inngest → triage → respond → DB `state='responded'` → LangFuse trace) that neither `/health` nor T-97 exercises end-to-end. The lesson stack behind this is now three deep — T-71, FQ-69, and FQ-70 were all "a green health signal while the real path was 100% broken." **(Track B)** Deepen eval coverage now that the live gate exists and blocks per-test regressions: grow each product eval past ADR-0007 §5.4's own small-N caveat, and vet additional model aliases for `triage`/`respond` the way T-96 did for `kb_learn` — both ride the now-live gate's admission path (ADR §8). Hardening/coverage sprint, not a feature sprint. Deliberately scoped small (anchor + one parallel eval track) — the same overcommit discipline Sprints 6–9 held.
**Sprint window:** August 6–20, 2026 (nominal, 2-week cadence from Sprint 9's Aug 6 end; note actual delivery has been compressing well ahead of window — Sprints 8/9 both effectively landed same-week as planning).
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening, same posture as Sprints 6–9. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Feeding retro:** `docs/retros/sprint-9.md` (authored 2026-07-12). T-98 executes that retro's §7 anchor + §5.2 standing lesson; Track B executes §7's eval-depth + additional-alias carries. §5.1's "security-review-before-implementing any credential change" norm applies to any key re-scope Track B needs.

**Standing norm reaffirmed this sprint (Sprint 9 §5.1):** **any credential / secret-store change — new key, DB role, re-scope, or secret — gets a fresh Security Lead review of the concrete payload/scope BEFORE implementation, with a T-90-style negative-test readback as proof.** Validated three times in Sprint 9 (T-90 / T-93 writer role / T-96 re-widen), each catching a distinct real risk. If Track B's additional-alias vetting needs the eval key re-scoped, that review is a hard gate, not a formality.

## Sprint 9 — ✅ COMPLETE (2026-07-12) — Real LLM-Rubric Eval Gate (build) + Monitoring Hardening

**Sprint:** Sprint 9 — Real LLM-Rubric Eval Gate (build) + Monitoring Hardening (capability build)
**Sprint goal:** Build the "real" LLM-rubric eval gate designed in ADR-0007 (Accepted, Tech Lead review appended) — the gate that finally makes CLAUDE.md's "eval-gated: no prompt change ships without passing a live >95% suite" constraint *true* instead of schema-validation-only. Ship it as the design specifies: a path-filtered live `llm-rubric` run against each function's real LiteLLM target alias, calibration-guarded so a broken harness fails loud (the T-84 lesson), reporting to `eval_gate_runs` + LangFuse, and enforced as a required merge-blocking check — using a scoped, budget-capped LiteLLM **virtual** key, never the master key. In parallel, close the monitoring blind spot Sprint 8's FQ-69 exposed the hard way (a rejected internal auth key that a green `/health/litellm` structurally could not see), and cash in the now-unblocked KB Learn allowlist unpin (T-84/T-88 delivered the 100% pass that gated it).
**Sprint window:** July 23 – August 6, 2026
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability-building, same posture as Sprints 6–8. The **Milestone numbering note** still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Design of record:** `docs/adr/0007-real-eval-gate.md` — **Accepted** (merged to `main`, PR #354; Evals Lead design rationale + Tech Lead CI/architecture review both appended). The Sprint 9 build is sized **medium** by that review (§7); the four Tech Lead build conditions **C1–C4** (ADR "Conditions / residuals") are folded into the tasks below as exit criteria, not left as prose.

**Why medium, not a research spike:** the hard part is already solved once in `run-kb-learn-eval.yml` (T-88's corrected harness — provider swap → `openai:chat:<alias>`, system prompt delivered as a real system-role message, grader through LiteLLM). No new database schema is *required* (`eval_gate_runs` exists, T-58) and no new external service (promptfoo, LiteLLM, LangFuse, GitHub Actions all in the stack). The novel surface is the calibration harness + the CI trigger security posture — several small-to-medium pieces with one load-bearing review gate, comparable in shape to a Sprint-7 track.

**Critical path:** T-89 (generalize T-88's harness into a shared live-run runner) → T-91 (calibration guards) + T-92 (per-test baseline store + green baseline capture) → T-93 (CI wiring — **sibling** workflow, stays on `workflow_dispatch`) → T-94 (register required check + nightly — founder/admin, build tail) → T-95 (docs/allowlist reconciliation, only once the gate is live). **The one hard build-ordering edge (Tech Lead C1):** the scoped budget-capped LiteLLM virtual key (**T-90**, Production Manager provisions + Security Lead signs off) **gates the auto `pull_request` trigger** — until `LITELLM_EVAL_KEY` exists, the live run stays on `workflow_dispatch`, and the master key must never enter the auto-triggered job's `env`. T-96 (KB Learn unpin) rides the gate once live (ADR §8). T-97 (internal-auth monitor) is independent and parallel.

**Founder-gated / carried-forward (no team task consumes sprint capacity — carried, not dropped):**
- **T-94 branch-protection required-check registration + nightly drift `schedule:`** — a genuine founder/admin action, but **mechanical** and due only at the *build tail* (after a green baseline exists). Do NOT file it now; file the FQ when the build reaches that step. Listed here so it isn't a surprise.
- **The concrete scoped virtual key's scope/cap/provisioning (T-90)** — a Security Lead + Production Manager joint sign-off at build time (per ADR deciders list + ADR-0006 T-B4 precedent). Team-owned, not a founder business decision. ✅ **Complete 2026-07-10** — both halves recorded (DECISIONS.md 2026-07-10); T-90 closed.
- **Per-user session auth (T-77 Option A)** — deferred; write surface accepts the single shared Basic Auth credential (`audit_log.actor = "dashboard"`). Revisit on a second dashboard user or a SOC-2 per-human-attribution need. Carried, not scheduled.
- **FQ-63** (staging dashboard real-TLS domain) — non-blocking cosmetic upgrade; founder action only, still open.
- **FQ-47 action 4b** (UptimeRobot paid-tier auto-incident posting) — deferred per free-tier-first; status page is live and manually updatable.
- **DNC / second-tenant onboarding** — deferred indefinitely per FQ-43 (founder decision); revisit only on founder signal.

**Explicitly deferred / flagged (not in scope, do not start early):**
- **Synthetic downstream-triage E2E monitor** (Sprint 6 §7 / Sprint 8 §7 risk — inject a synthetic ticket, assert it triages end-to-end). Larger than T-97's internal-auth probe and **partly subsumed by it** + the FQ-69 real-data-drain evidence. PM call: **not committed this sprint** — kept a flagged carry; revisit once T-97 lands and we see whether the auth probe closes enough of the gap. (Decision recorded in DECISIONS.md.)
- **Growing each eval to ≥20 tests** (ADR §5.4 option a) — good coverage hygiene worth doing regardless, but a slower ongoing effort, not this sprint's anchor. The gate uses **baseline-relative** (§5.4 option b) so it does not depend on this.
- **Root-cause-of-the-root-cause of the master-key divergence** (how litellm-prod's key rotated without propagating to ops-hub-prod) — flagged, non-blocking; partly mitigated by T-97.
- **`LITELLM_URL` Coolify duplicate-row dedup** — cosmetic (both rows hold the identical correct value); opportunistic, not scheduled.

| T-91: Add calibration guards to the shared runner (ADR §5 + §6 step 3 / **C4**) | Evals Lead | T-89 | ✅ **DONE (2026-07-10, PR #366).** Three ADR-0007 §5 guards added to the shared runner — new **`scripts/eval/calibration-guards.py`** (`token-band` / `canary-check` / `grader-target`) + three **`evals/canaries/{ticket-triage,ticket-respond,kb-learn}-canary.yaml`** fixtures, wired into **`scripts/eval/live-run.sh`** to run automatically on every invocation. **(1) Per-eval token band** (Finding 5): `floor = user_max + 0.30·sys`, `ceil = 2.5·(sys+user_max)`, derived from each eval's own reference size — bands genuinely differ (triage `[124,520]`, respond `[191,943]`, kb-learn `[405,2500]`), so a global `≥600` would both false-trip triage/respond **and** miss a collapse there; a collapse toward user-only tokens (the T-84 `config.system`-dropped signature) or missing/zero usage = **hard error (exit 2)**, never a rate on bad data. **(2) Canaries** (§5.2): each eval carries one must-pass + one must-fail (`metadata.canary`); the must-fail rubric demands an impossible sentinel a correct model never emits, so a correct grader must fail it — must-fail-passes (rubber-stamp) or must-pass-fails (harness broken) = **hard error (exit 4)**. Rule = "zero regressions vs last green baseline," keyed on per-test `<eval>::<description>`. **Fail-closed on the two swap-holes the advisor flagged:** a baselined test that PASSED and now FAILS blocks; a baselined test that's ABSENT from the current run (dropped/errored/renamed) blocks; a pre-existing failing-and-waived test does not re-block; a new-and-failing test warns loudly (blocks only under `--strict-new`). **Validated locally on 5 synthetic cases incl. the decisive swap (3/4→3/4 same count, coarse would PASS, per-test BLOCKS on the regressed test).** Writer `recordEvalGateRun` extended with `caseResults` (JSONB-serialized) + unit test; full suite 176 passed.<br>**ADR §7 "no new schema" is now CONDITIONAL — named** (as the task requires): one nullable JSONB column. the only healthy scoped config — `fallback-model` is broken on staging, FQ-70) → `compare-baseline.py capture` → baseline artifact. **✅ CAPTURED GREEN: 12/12 (all score 1.0) — kb-learn 4/4, ticket-respond 4/4, ticket-triage 4/4 (the previously-live-unverified one, now confirmed) — [run 29068118128](https://github.com/admin-nutshell/ops-hub-00/actions/runs/29068118128), git_sha `4701fdb`, artifact `eval-baseline-4701fdb…`.** End-to-end re-proven on the real captured data: `compare-baseline.py compare baseline vs the same run` → 12 baselined / 12 current, all stable, **GATE PASS (exit 0)**. **Deferred + named honestly:** (a) the `eval_gate_runs` baseline row needs FQ-71 applied + a CI DB cred (T-93); (b) "record in LangFuse" has **no existing eval→LangFuse mechanism** to follow — durable baseline evidence this session = the capture run permalink + artifact + the deferred DB row; (c) grader≠target (T-91) needs a 2nd healthy judge alias — baseline MUST be re-captured under the real config before the gate blocks — and since the real gate runs grader≠target (T-91), that re-capture is mandatory anyway, so it *subsumes* the deferred DB-row write: the `eval_gate_runs` row gets written when the baseline is re-captured under the real config post-FQ-71, not as an orphan copy-paste step.<br>**Seam fix (advisor-caught, PR #368): flat-vs-nested baseline shape.** `capture` stores per-test data as a **flat array** (`eval_gate_runs.case_results` / the `caseResults` payload), but `compare` originally read the baseline **only** as a nested `{evals:{…}}` doc — so once T-93 materializes the DB row (flat) and feeds it to `compare`, the reader would see **zero baselined tests and PASS EVERYTHING** (the swap-masking dead-gate T-92 exists to close, reopened one seam over). Fixed: `compare` now normalizes **all three** baseline shapes (nested capture doc / DB-row `{case_results:[…]}` / bare flat array) via `_load_baseline_map`, and **fails closed on an empty/malformed baseline** (refuses to green-light against zero tests). New stdlib regression test `scripts/eval/test_compare_baseline.py` (9 cases) proves a swap **blocks under the flat DB-row shape**, dropped-test fails closed, and empty baseline blocks — the exact case the file-round-trip tests structurally couldn't exercise. Recorded in DECISIONS.md 2026-07-09 T-92. | Aug 1 |

PASSWORD` needs service_role/owner privilege no agent holds (non-negotiable #3), and the obvious "one-click GitHub workflow" turns out to be unsafe: it would need a service_role-class DSN sitting as a persistent Actions secret (recreating the exact O1 footgun the T-93 credential review flagged) and `workflow_dispatch` **inputs are shown unmasked** in the run UI/API, so the DSN can't ride an input either. **Security Lead ruling (DECISIONS.md 2026-07-10): Option A (GitHub-Actions-automated) REJECTED; Option B (founder SQL-Editor single paste, same channel as every prior FQ this sprint) APPROVED**, with 3 refinements — password generated server-side (pgcrypto, never a literal in the saved query text), applied via a `pg_temp` function's `EXECUTE format(...)` (avoids a logged top-level `ALTER ROLE ... PASSWORD` DDL statement), and the assembled DSN returned via a plain `SELECT` result (not a `RAISE NOTICE`, which can mirror to server logs) — built exactly to spec as **`supabase/ops/t93_set_eval_gate_ci_writer_password.sql`** (NOT a migration — no DDL on any table — kept for provenance/re-run-to-rotate). **FQ-73 filed**: ONE founder sitting, two actions (run the SQL Editor script once → copy the one result cell → paste into GitHub Settings → Secrets → Actions as `EVAL_GATE_DB_URL`). **(2) The INSERT wiring itself — DONE, landed regardless of the password gap** (task explicitly authorized this): `compare-baseline.py capture` gained `--payload-out` (writes the exact `recordEvalGateRun`-shaped JSON to a file; 2 new stdlib tests, 11/11 passing) and a `--workflow-run-url` default derived from `GITHUB_SERVER_URL`/`GITHUB_REPOSITORY`/`GITHUB_RUN_ID`. ## Sprint 8 — ✅ COMPLETE (2026-07-09) — Drift Reconciliation + Eval Coverage

**Sprint:** Sprint 8 — Drift Reconciliation + Eval Coverage (debt-paydown / hardening)
**Sprint goal:** Close the class of live-vs-record **drift** that both Sprint 6 and Sprint 7 kept surfacing the hard way — starting with a one-shot reconciliation of every live `pg_policy` row against what our migration files *should* have created (the same botched 2026-06-22 apply has now lost `kb_articles_write` **and** `feature_flags_write`; do not find instance #3 in production). In parallel, close the two eval-coverage gaps we've flagged repeatedly but never scheduled: write the missing **KB Learn prompt eval** (the only agent function with zero eval coverage, which is why its model allowlist is pinned to a single option), and produce a **design-of-record ADR for the "real" LLM-rubric eval gate** so it stops being flagged-twice-and-never-scheduled. Finish the one genuine carry from Sprint 6 (T-62 freeze-schema + QA E2E). This is deliberately a hardening sprint, not a feature sprint — it directly executes both retros' #1 process change.
**Sprint window:** July 9–23, 2026
**Target milestone:** None declared — capability/hardening work, same posture as Sprints 6–7. The **Milestone numbering note** (Sprint 6/7 headers below) still stands: do NOT label this work M7. Charter-M7 is gated on an exogenous tenant-onboarding event that hasn't happened (FQ-43, DNC deferred indefinitely). Revisit numbering only on a founder decision that reopens tenant onboarding.
**Retros feeding this sprint:** `docs/retros/sprint-6.md` and `docs/retros/sprint-7.md` (both authored 2026-07-09). T-83 executes both retros' process-change #1 (proactive drift reconciliation); T-87 executes Sprint 7's carried eval-gate gap; the deploy-verify SHA-assertion discipline (Sprint 7 §5.3) applies to any redeploy this sprint.

**Why the "real" eval gate is a design spike here, not a build:** building the LLM-rubric quality gate (ADR-0006 T-B1 option b) is plausibly a whole sprint on its own — CI integration, cost model, rubric authoring, threshold calibration, and a live pass path. Pairing the full build with the reconciliation + KB Learn eval + T-62 closeout would repeat exactly the Sprint 5 overcommit pattern this team keeps deliberately avoiding. So Sprint 8 produces the **decision-of-record ADR** (sizing, approach, CI design, cost) via T-87; the build targets Sprint 9. Deferring the build is the disciplined call, not a punt — it's scheduled, scoped, and named, which is more than it's ever had.

**Critical path:** mostly parallel (distinct owners, no bandwidth conflict — same shape as Sprint 6's parallel tracks). The one real chain is the sprint anchor: **T-83 read-only `pg_policy` diff → (if gaps found) Security-Lead-reviewed fix migration → founder apply via SQL Editor → re-verify.** T-84, T-85, T-86, T-87 each run independently.

**Founder-gated / carried-forward (no team task consumes sprint capacity — carried, not dropped):**
- **T-76 Advisory C1** (non-blocking hardening) — revoke write verbs from `authenticated`/`anon` on `agent_model_routing`. Not scheduled as its own task; **if T-83 produces a fix migration anyway, fold C1's grant-revoke into that same migration** (one Security Lead review + one founder apply instead of two — a real founder-cycle saving). Flagged so it isn't silently dropped.
- **Per-user session auth (T-77 Option A)** — deferred; write surface accepts the single shared Basic Auth credential (`audit_log.actor = "dashboard"`). Revisit when a second dashboard user is added or a SOC-2 audit needs per-human attribution. Carried, not scheduled.
- **FQ-63** (staging dashboard real-TLS domain) — non-blocking cosmetic upgrade; founder action only, still open.
- **FQ-47 action 4b** (UptimeRobot paid-tier auto-incident posting) — deferred per free-tier-first; status page is live and manually updatable.
- **DNC / second-tenant onboarding** — deferred indefinitely per FQ-43 (founder decision); revisit only on founder signal.

**Explicitly deferred to Sprint 9 (not in scope, do not start early):**
- **The "real" LLM-rubric eval gate build** — Sprint 8 produces only its ADR (T-87). Building it is Sprint 9 scope, sized by that ADR.
- **Unpinning KB Learn's model allowlist to a real multi-model choice** — mechanically gated on T-84's eval existing and passing (>95%) first; the eval is the unblock, the widening is the follow-on.
- **A synthetic downstream-triage monitor** (Sprint 6 §7 risk — a green `/health` didn't catch T-71's 100%-failing triage). Worth doing, not scoped here; carried as a known gap.

| T-84: Author `evals/kb-learn.yaml` — close the KB Learn prompt-eval coverage gap | Evals Lead | — | ✅ **DONE (2026-07-09).** `evals/kb-learn.yaml` authored (PR #337) — 4 `llm-rubric` tests @0.8 (faithful extraction / identifier-stripping / no-hallucination / injection-resistance). **First live run against `triage-model`, run [28995361450](https://github.com/admin-nutshell/ops-hub-00/actions/runs/28995361450): 1/4 passed (25%).** ⚠️ **CORRECTION (found during T-88, do not treat the 25% as a confirmed production vulnerability):** the run harness had a real bug — it copied the system prompt into the swapped-in `openai:chat:triage-model` provider's `config.system` field, but **the openai-compatible provider ignores `config.system`** (only the anthropic reference provider honors it). Token-count evidence: that run's 4 calls totaled 497 prompt tokens (~124/call) — the ~850-token system prompt reached **zero** of them. So the 25% result measured a model with **no system prompt at all**, not KB Learn's actual configured behavior — production's real code path (`generateKbArticle`) sends the system message correctly via the messages array, so the original prompt was never confirmed exploitable under a correct measurement. The blast-radius check (read-only, PR #342 — dumped all 5 existing `kb_articles` rows, zero PII-pattern flags) still stands as reassurance regardless. **Net effect:** this task closes with a real, working eval + a real, if less dramatic than first reported, motivation for hardening — routed to T-88, which fixed the harness bug itself and confirmed **100% (4/4) pass, twice**, against the hardened prompt via the corrected harness. | Jul 17 |
| T-88: Harden KB Learn's system prompt (injection resistance, PII redaction, JSON reliability) + code-level PII guard | Tech Lead (prompt + guard) | T-84 finding | ✅ **DONE (2026-07-09) — 100% (4/4) pass, twice, against the real production model.** PR #344. **Prompt hardened** (`src/inngest/kb-learn.ts` + `evals/kb-learn.yaml`'s reference block kept byte-identical, per that file's own invariant): explicit non-negotiable injection-resistance framing (never follow embedded instructions, never abandon the JSON contract regardless of ticket content), enumerated PII categories + a "generalize, don't just omit" imperative, stricter JSON-only instruction + two few-shot examples (one exercising redaction+injection+shape together, one a sparse-ticket no-hallucination case so the few-shot itself doesn't regress that test). **Defense-in-depth code guard added** (not prompt-only): `generateKbArticle()` re-scans the parsed `title`/`body` for PII-shaped patterns (email, ticket-ID, phone-number runs) **after** JSON parse but **before** the caller's INSERT, and throws (same fail-closed path as a parse failure) if any hit — independent of prompt quality, so a future prompt/model regression can't silently persist PII again; error names only the identifier *kind*, never the leaked value. **+10 new unit tests** (`kb-learn.test.ts`, now 15 cases) — clean-pass, per-PII-kind rejection, and a false-positive guard (HTTP status codes aren't mistaken for phone numbers). Full suite 175 passed / 27 skipped. **Real bug found and fixed en route:** the T-84 run harness itself had the `config.system`-ignored-by-openai-provider bug described above — fixed by delivering the system prompt as a real system-role message via a generated prompt function, which is *why* this task could get a valid pass-rate number at all. **Verified twice, not once** (temp-0.2 flakiness ruled out): [run 28997680312](https://github.com/admin-nutshell/ops-hub-00/actions/runs/28997680312) and [run 28997984109](https://github.com/admin-nutshell/ops-hub-00/actions/runs/28997984109), both 4/4 (100%), both ~853 prompt tokens/call confirming the system prompt is genuinely reaching the model this time. **Follow-up flagged, not scheduled:** the same `config.system`-on-openai-provider bug class could affect any future live-run override written for the other evals — worth a check when one is next authored. | Jul 17 |

It does strengthen the finding one way: litellm-prod being reachable externally rules out "litellm is just down" as an alternative explanation. Then, following the advisor's push for real behavioral evidence (not just config diffing), dispatched the existing read-only `verify-agent-cost-feed.yml` (trace_name=ticket-triage, lookback=1d) against real LangFuse Cloud data — [run 29022632064](https://github.com/admin-nutshell/ops-hub-00/actions/runs/29022632064): **14,800 matching `ticket-triage` traces in the last 24h**, sampled page of 20 all `project_id=00…0003`/`tenant_id=00…0030` (prod), timestamps clustered in tight ~10-trace bursts roughly 3 minutes apart (e.g. 13:42:0x–13:42:2x, then 13:45:2x–13:45:3x), against a small repeating set of ~8–9 distinct `ticket_id`s (`0bb90013…`, `3f8c6a46…`, `095c899f…`, `8ec24451…`, `d3bfb9c6…`, `9ea9969e…`, `3c9427cc…`, `e86b7abd…`, `1d5a62f9…`). Cross-referenced against code: `triageOneTicket`'s idempotency guard (`ticket-triage.ts` line ~175) returns `{skipped:true}` **before** any LangFuse trace is created for tickets already past `state='new'` — so a trace only exists when a REAL attempt was made against a ticket still in `'new'`. The only mechanism that repeatedly re-dispatches the SAME small set of tickets on a ~5-min cadence is `sweepNewTickets` (`ticket-triage.ts` line ~292, `*/5 * * * *` cron, scoped by `STAGING_PROJECT_ID`/`STAGING_TENANT_ID` — misleadingly named constants that actually resolve to `POLLING_PROJECT_ID`/`POLLING_TENANT_ID`, i.e. prod's real ids on ops-hub-prod), combined with Inngest's built-in `retries:2` per dispatch. That pattern (small fixed ticket set, repeating every ~3–5 min, indefinitely, all real attempts) is the exact signature of tickets stuck in `state='new'` because every `classifyTicket` call is throwing before the `UPDATE ... SET state='triaged'` — consistent with, and best explained by, the confirmed-stale internal `LITELLM_URL` (`getaddrinfo EAI_AGAIN`, same as T-71). **Did not pull the raw LangFuse generation error text or query live ticket rows to get 100% direct confirmation** — deliberately avoided using `SUPABASE_STAGING_DB_URL` (a superuser/RLS-bypass credential) to read real prod ticket content for this, since that's outside this check's justified scope and adjacent to the CLAUDE.md #3 service_role-at-runtime constraint in spirit; the LangFuse-count/pattern evidence plus the independently-confirmed URL mismatch is treated as high-confidence, not proven-to-certainty. **Bottom line: real production support tickets (~8-9 of them, prod scope) are very likely stuck un-triaged and un-responded right now**, repeatedly failing and being re-swept every few minutes, since at least the freeze-schema restart. This is a live customer-impacting incident, not a latent risk — escalated accordingly (FQ-69, upgraded). **Other pre-flight facts confirmed clean:** `POLLING_PROJECT_ID=00…0003`/`POLLING_TENANT_ID=00…0030` correct on ops-hub-prod (per T-60's live env audit); `/health` and `/health/env` both 200 on ops-hub-prod (`checked:14, missing:[]`) — env-var *presence* is fine, the *value* is what's stale; `respondTicket` confirmed to post an internal FreeScout NOTE only (type=3), never an outbound customer email, so injecting a test ticket carries no risk of emailing a real stranger; `triageTicket` confirmed to auto-dispatch `ops-hub/ticket.respond` on success (`ticket-triage.ts` line ~270) — full pipeline wiring is live, contrary to a stale dormant-function comment in `ticket-respond.ts`.<br>**Attempted to hand the fix to Production Manager** (the guarded `fix-ops-hub-prod-litellm-url.yml` workflow already exists for exactly this failure mode — `confirm_container_name` input, deletes duplicate rows, sets one correct value, restarts, polls health) — **blocked by the harness's own permission classifier**: dispatching a production env-var mutation + restart requires explicit user/founder authorization, even via agent-to-agent handoff. Did not attempt to work around this. **Exit, updated:** founder/Production-Manager authorizes + runs `fix-ops-hub-prod-litellm-url.yml confirm_container_name=hlik1d96uvkkjzpbxa3azhcv-132650269773` (re-confirm the container name fresh first — it may move again) → re-verify `/health` 200 + exactly one `LITELLM_URL` row → QA injects a real ticket via FreeScout (mechanism: T-51 used a real test email; this session did not yet attempt injection at all, so the FreeScout-side mechanism is still open — real email preferred, FreeScout REST-API-created customer-thread conversation as fallback per this task's own guidance, direct DB insert as freescout_user as last resort only) → confirm `state=responded` in Supabase + a LangFuse `ticket-respond`/`ticket-triage` trace (not just a state flip) + reply visible in FreeScout UI → T-62/T-85/FQ-57 all close together.<br><br>**UPDATE (2026-07-09, same day, user-authorized):** user explicitly authorized dispatching `fix-ops-hub-prod-litellm-url.yml`.
